DIY

How to perfectly rip = off the=20 Tablebeast TB-SK01

modified Casio SK-1=20 Synthesizer

[Page 1] [Page 2] [Page 3] [Page 4] [Home]

 

Step 3:=20 Prepping

Flip over your Sk-1 to expose the underside. Get your = screwdriver=20 out and take out the 11 screws residing in the case. Place them in a cup = or jar=20 otherwise you will lose them.

Open up the beast and flip the bottom of the case over. = To make=20 everything easier for yourself, go ahead and clip the power leads from = the=20 battery compartment to the circuit board. Be sure to leave enough of a = tail on=20 the wire on the circuit board to ensure you remember which is red and = which is=20 black and where it is. Matter of fact, go ahead and mark on the circuit = board=20 with he sharpie R for red and B for black just in case. This will make = the mod=20 go much easier, trust me I would know.

Take the four screws out off of the speaker, cut the = leads, and=20 then do whatever you want with it: throw it away, make an array out of = 50 of=20 them, put them in a toy car, choke on it, who cares. Just get rid of it, = because=20 it is taking up valuable internal space.

 

Step 4: = Marking, Cutting, and=20 Mounting

Put the two halves of the case back together and flip = the unit=20 back over. Find the now vacant speaker compartment on the left of the = unit as=20 pictured (pretty hard to miss). You can measure the space you will need = without=20 the aid of a ruler, but if you must, go right ahead. from the edges of = the=20 speaker channels, measure a 1/4" in on both sides, this will center up = the patch=20 panels. Now draw a line from the bottom of the top set of channels down = to the=20 top of the seventh channel of the bottom section, as pictured. Now draw = a line=20 with your sharpie connecting the two sides with a top and bottom line, = following=20 these channels. I know it sounds confusing, but just look at the picture = and it=20 will all be clear.

Before you drill be sure that you are not going to = contact the=20 ground wires for the keys or the huge output capacitor with whatever you = are=20 cutting with. Just drill barely as deep as you need to avoid destroying = any of=20 the vital internal components. Be very careful, whatever you do. Now, = cut this=20 section out, following the sharpie marks, and throw away the cut out = piece.

GO back and clean up any edges that are not perfect and = check the=20 hole you cut by placing the two panels in place, making sure that none = of the=20 parts interfere with each other. The panels should mount flat and neat. = Trim any=20 excess interfering areas.

Now, you are going to line up the two patch panels in = the cut out=20 space. I line them up by centering the pair and using the very edge of = the=20 fourth channel to keep it straight. Drill one hole at a time and be sure = to put=20 a screw through each hole as a placeholder as you drill. That way you = can be=20 sure of the neatness of your layout. I usually go in diagonal order. = From bottom=20 left to top right, then reverse for the adjacent panel, and finally = filling in=20 the last four holes. That way if you make a mistake for placement you = still have=20 a few other holes you can re drill. Just work slow and carefully on this = part=20 whatever method you choose to use, as the quality of this will be the = most=20 obvious part of the mod, make sure it looks good!

Secure the 3/4", 6/32 Machine screws with matching nuts, = you can=20 use a nut driver, pliers, vise-grip, whatever to do this.

Be careful with the top left corner here so as your = mounting screw=20 does not interfere with the circuit-board or parts on it.To get the = screw into=20 this tight place you can either take all of the screws out of the = circuit board=20 and flop it over or put a nut on the tip of a small screwdriver and hold = it in=20 place from above.

Now in the four areas below the speaker hole is where = you will put=20 the helper section switches. Mark 1/4" for each hole if mini style = switches are=20 used. Center the holes up as shown in the left pic where the red arrows = are and=20 be sure to trim any excess interfering plastic from the case as shown in = the=20 middle pic. Test each hole with a switch, then when it is nice and snug, = not=20 loose or too tight, secure each switch with the accompanying nut and a = single=20 lock washer, as there is not really enough thread on most switches for = both=20 washer and lock washer.

Measure about halfway between the two mounting screws a = hole large=20 enough for your 1/4" output jack. cut it where it will not interfere = with your=20 new patchbay and you should be fine, just look at the pics for = placement.

Looking good! Now, the cosmetic steps of this project = are=20 completed from the basic standpoint. Here you could co on to paint, = mark, lebel,=20 or do whatever you want to modify the unit visually. I don't do anything = because=20 I like the basic look, though I have done extensive decorating in the = past. My=20 advice is do whatever you want with it, have fun. Make the mod as = obvious or=20 stealh as you wish. Now onto the soldering.
